# Fault Localization: HDA Intel Sound Fails After Suspend to RAM

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/linux--07c4ee00 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/linux--07c4ee00 (mirror of torvalds/linux)
- **Kernel Version**: 3.7.6
- **Difficulty**: expert
- **Category**: fault_localization
- **Subsystem**: Drivers
- **Component**: Sound (HDA Intel)

## Bug Report

**Bug ID**: 53441
**Summary**: hda_intel: sound stops working after suspend to ram
**Regression**: Yes (works on v3.6.11, broken since v3.7.1)

On a fresh boot the sound card works fine. After a few suspends to ram (it doesn't necessarily happen after just one) the sound card stops working well. The sound comes out choppy, as a series of clicks separated by 2 second or so silences.

I see these messages in the kernel log right after resume:
```
hda-intel: azx_get_response timeout, switching to polling mode: last cmd=0x00170503
hda-intel: No response from codec, disabling MSI: last cmd=0x00170503
hda_intel: azx_get_response timeout, switching to single_cmd mode: last cmd=0x00170503
```

The only way to fix the sound seems to be a reboot. I don't have this problem with v3.6.11, it appeared with kernel v3.7.1 (I have not tested v3.7). Right now I'm running 3.7.6 and the problem is still there.

```
$ lspci | grep -i audio
00:1b.0 Audio device: Intel Corporation 5 Series/3400 Series Chipset High Definition Audio (rev 05)
01:00.1 Audio device: NVIDIA Corporation High Definition Audio Controller (rev a1)

$ lsmod | grep snd
snd_hda_codec_hdmi     24993  4
snd_hda_codec_idt      54740  1
snd_hda_intel          24840  6
snd_hda_codec          71155  3 snd_hda_codec_hdmi,snd_hda_codec_idt,snd_hda_intel
snd_pcm                74322  3 snd_hda_codec_hdmi,snd_hda_codec,snd_hda_intel
snd_page_alloc          7333  2 snd_pcm,snd_hda_intel
snd_timer              17563  1 snd_pcm
```

## Task

You are a fault localization agent. Given the bug report above, your task is to identify the **exact source file(s)** and **function(s)/data structure(s)** in the Linux kernel source tree (at `/workspace`) that need to be modified to fix this bug.

You must:
1. Analyze the bug report to understand the symptoms and context
2. Search the kernel source code to identify the relevant subsystem and files
3. Narrow down to the specific file(s) and function(s)/data structure(s) that contain the bug or need modification
4. Write your findings to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json` in the following format:

```json
{
  "buggy_files": ["path/to/file.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["function_or_struct_name"],
  "confidence": 0.8,
  "reasoning": "Brief explanation of why these locations are the fault"
}
```

**Important**: Paths should be relative to the kernel source root (e.g., `kernel/sched/core.c`, not `/workspace/kernel/sched/core.c`).

## Success Criteria

57-assistanttext-
Now I have a clear understanding of the bug. Let me document my findings and then run a test to verify:

**Root Cause Analysis:**

The bug occurs because:
1. When a codec timeout occurs before suspend, `chip->polling_mode` is set to 1 (line 912) or `chip->single_cmd` is set to 1 (line 951)
2. During suspend, `azx_stop_chip()` is called which sets `chip->initialized = 0` but does NOT reset `polling_mode` or `single_cmd`
3. During resume, `azx_init_chip()` is called but has an early return if `chip->initialized` is already 1 (line 1211)
4. More critically, `azx_init_chip()` only reinitializes the CORB/RIRB if `chip->single_cmd` is 0 (line 1222-1223)
5. If `single_cmd` is still 1 from previous error recovery, the codec command I/O never gets reinitialized
6. This causes codec communication to fail immediately after resume

The fix is to reset `chip->polling_mode` to 0 in `azx_init_chip()` when a full reset is requested.

88-assistanttext-
Perfect! I have successfully completed the fault localization analysis for the HDA Intel sound driver bug. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Fault Localization Complete

**File**: `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`

### Key Findings:

1. **Buggy File**: `sound/pci/hda/hda_intel.c`
2. **Buggy Function**: `azx_init_chip()` (line 1209)
3. **Confidence**: 0.95 (very high)

### Root Cause:

The `azx_init_chip()` function fails to reset error recovery state variables (`chip->polling_mode` and `chip->poll_count`) when performing a full reset during resume operations.

### Problem Flow:

1. **Before suspend**: A codec timeout triggers error recovery that sets `polling_mode=1`
2. **During suspend**: `azx_stop_chip()` resets `initialized=0` but **NOT** `polling_mode` or `poll_count`
3. **During resume**: `azx_init_chip(chip, 1)` is called, but `polling_mode` remains 1
4. **Result**: All subsequent codec communications are forced through the polling/error recovery path instead of normal operation, causing immediate timeouts and the observed error messages

### Why This Appeared in v3.7.1+:

The regression appeared between v3.6.11 (working) and v3.7.1 (broken), suggesting changes to the resume/reset handling code path removed or missed resetting these error recovery state flags.

### Required Fix:

Reset `chip->polling_mode=0` and `chip->poll_count=0` in `azx_init_chip()` when `full_reset` is requested, before line 1215.

*/\n742: \tazx_writew(chip, CORBWP, 0);\n743: \t/* reset the corb hw read pointer */\n744: \tazx_writew(chip, CORBRP, ICH6_CORBRP_RST);\n745: \t/* enable corb dma */\n746: \tazx_writeb(chip, CORBCTL, %= ICH6_MAX_CORB_ENTRIES;\n816: \n817: \tchip->rirb.cmds[addr]++;\n818: \tchip->corb.buf[wp] = cpu_to_le32(val);\n819: \tazx_writel(chip, CORBWP, wp);\n820: \n821: \tspin_unlock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n822: \n823: \treturn 0;\n824: }\n825: \n826: #define ICH6_RIRB_EX_UNSOL_EV\t(1<<4)\n827: \n828: /* retrieve RIRB entry - called from interrupt handler */\n829: static void azx_update_rirb(struct azx *chip)\n830: {\n831: \tunsigned int rp, wp;\n832: \tunsigned int addr;\n833: \tu32 res, res_ex;\n834: \n835: \twp = azx_readb(chip, RIRBWP);\n836: \tif (wp == azx_rirb_get_response(struct hda_bus *bus,\n864: \t\t\t\t\t  unsigned int addr)\n865: {\n866: \tstruct azx *chip = bus->private_data;\n867: \tunsigned long timeout;\n868: \tunsigned long || do_poll) {\n876: \t\t\tspin_lock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n877: \t\t\tazx_update_rirb(chip);\n878: \t\t\tspin_unlock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n879: \t\t}\n880: \t\tif (!chip->rirb.cmds[addr]) {\n881: \tif (!chip->polling_mode) {\n909: \t\tsnd_printk(KERN_WARNING SFX \"azx_get_response timeout, \"\n910: \t\t\t   \"switching to polling mode: last cmd=0x%08x\\n\",\n911: \t\t\t The command was\n964:  *       intended for the BIOS only, and may get confused with unsolicited\n965:  *       responses.  So, we shouldn't use it for normal operation from the\n966:  *       driver.\n967:  *       I left the codes, however, for debugging/testing purposes.\n968:  */\n969: \n970: /* receive a response */\n971: static int azx_single_wait_for_response(struct azx *chip, unsigned int addr)\n972: {\n973: \tint timeout = 50;\n974: \n975: \twhile (timeout--) {\n976: \t\t/* check IRV busy bit */\n977: azx_power_notify(struct hda_bus *bus, bool power_up);\n1062: #endif\n1063: \n1064: /* reset codec link */\n1065: static int azx_reset(struct azx *chip, int full_reset)\n1066: {\n1067: \tint */\n1076: \tazx_writel(chip, GCTL, azx_readl(chip, GCTL) & ~ICH6_GCTL_RESET);\n1077: \n1078: \tcount = 50;\n1079: \twhile (azx_readb(chip, GCTL) && --count)\n1080: \t\tmsleep(1);\n1081: \n1082: \t/* = 1;\n1230: }\n1231: \n1232: /*\n1233:  * initialize the PCI registers\n1234:  */\n1235: /* update bits in a PCI register byte */\n1236: static void update_pci_byte(struct pci_dev *pci, unsigned int When a codec timeout occurs before suspend, polling_mode is set to 1. During suspend, azx_stop_chip() is called which sets chip->initialized=0 but does NOT reset polling_mode. When a codec timeout occurs before suspend, polling_mode is set to 1. During suspend, azx_stop_chip() is called which sets chip->initialized=0 but does NOT reset polling_mode. During resume, azx_init_chip() is called with full_reset=1, but it fails to reset polling_mode back to 0.
